<span id="freeTextContainer6539948120654737458">In this book, almost everything happens “off-screen” so to speak, so—if you want the action this may not be the book for you. <br/><br/>It keeps you on the edge of your seat (somehow) as well as in the dark; so that you don’t know what happened until the end. Well, unless you can read between the lines and take hints OR unless you are super intuitive. <br/>So, I found it good in one respect, and lacking in another. All of the major events were simply written around and the writing would happen before and then </span>
  <span id="freeText6539948120654737458" style="display:none">In this book, almost everything happens “off-screen” so to speak, so—if you want the action this may not be the book for you. <br /><br />It keeps you on the edge of your seat (somehow) as well as in the dark; so that you don’t know what happened until the end. Well, unless you can read between the lines and take hints OR unless you are super intuitive. <br />So, I found it good in one respect, and lacking in another. All of the major events were simply written around and the writing would happen before and then after them. I felt some of them were significant enough to write in, but I still liked the book. I just felt that half of it was missing and that there should have been more action and less time showing the characters freaking out.<br />HOWEVER; some ppl just don’t want the details. The gory details or the interesting stuff. I don’t know all that many of those ppl, but this is perfect for ppl who want to skip the grit. :D</span>

<div id="review_2120663060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120663060" />
    <a title="Nthambi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42888929-nthambi"><img alt="Nthambi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120663060?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nthambi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nthambi" href="/user/show/42888929-nthambi">Nthambi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2120663060&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120663060" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1783094479478326825">Chapter 4 and I am already seething!!!!!!! Ella must have a big problem if she thinks that Anna's disappearance is her fault, and everyone else who blames her is very hypocritical. I don't know the entire story yet, and I am not sure if I can withstand all these stupid feelings of guilt and blame to finish the book.<br/><br/>Decided to continue to Chapter 6, and I cannot understand how a woman who almost called a girl's parents (she did not know this girl from Adam) because said girl was interacting with </span>
  <span id="freeText1783094479478326825" style="display:none">Chapter 4 and I am already seething!!!!!!! Ella must have a big problem if she thinks that Anna's disappearance is her fault, and everyone else who blames her is very hypocritical. I don't know the entire story yet, and I am not sure if I can withstand all these stupid feelings of guilt and blame to finish the book.<br /><br />Decided to continue to Chapter 6, and I cannot understand how a woman who almost called a girl's parents (she did not know this girl from Adam) because said girl was interacting with an ex-convict she just met, would adamantly refuse to go to the police after receiving threatening messages. I mean, Ella has too much empathy and no sense of self-preservation!!!<br /><br />I am continuing this just so I can criticize it more...<br /><br />I have no idea how I feel about the book in general after finishing it. It was confusing that the entire concept of the phrase "I Am Watching You" came together within the last 10 pages of the book. The story does not invest enough of Tim's character to help a reader understand the progress of his obsessions and why he believed in what he did. <br /><br />Driscoll throws you around a lot with this tale, and by the time I was through, it felt pointless to have gone through all that. I could select only a handful of chapters to read and get the entire story without missing a thing. Instead of writing pages and pages about Mathews's family, why didn't Driscoll give us more on the murder suspects so that we can have fun at guessing who the perpetrator is? It would have been a wonderful pleasure to know these men and their shortcomings instead of being inside Ella's head which was no help at all.<br /><br />All those details into Ella's life and it is only in the last chapters when we get to know that she bumped into Tim on the train. Complete waste of time!!! Took me 5 days to read through this (way longer than it should have) because it is not the book that encourages you to read it through the night and convince yourself that you'll sleep later.<br /><br />I would not recommend this to anyone. It is a disappointment and not the kind of story that sticks with you days after you read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1783094479478326825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dsLH8vwsimRTAMdHjgbjOZyQc5FTJ1Ln+kaqwb7NtHKEVtpCQn94BwDJ5/kufH8m4s/S2WuZM7lXio6hi0PDCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JGQX+YVFcjbwX7NkFKDeqSvfFaeRh7oQ6dC945SVx5TW8ApJOxaAVaOWk9q02kK2VYC076k5205EHJmDoRuw7Q==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9824054138692991517">Teresa Driscoll - a former BBC TV news presenter- is now an international #1 bestselling author. Her debut psychological suspense I AM WATCHING YOU hit Number One on Kindle in the UK, USA and Australia and sold more than half a million copies in its first year. Her second thriller THE FRIEND was also Kindle #1 in the UK and Australia and a top #10 bestseller in the USA. <br/>Teresa also writes women's </span>
  <span id="freeText9824054138692991517" style="display:none">Teresa Driscoll - a former BBC TV news presenter- is now an international #1 bestselling author. Her debut psychological suspense I AM WATCHING YOU hit Number One on Kindle in the UK, USA and Australia and sold more than half a million copies in its first year. Her second thriller THE FRIEND was also Kindle #1 in the UK and Australia and a top #10 bestseller in the USA. <br />Teresa also writes women's fiction. Her debut in this genre RECIPES FOR MELISSA was auctioned at the Frankfurt book fair between seven German publishers and her second women's fiction title is LAST KISS GOODNIGHT.<br />During her long career as a journalist, Teresa worked for newspapers, magazines and television, including 15 years presenting the BBC TV news programme Spotlight. Covering crime for so long, she was deeply moved by the haunting impact on the relatives, the friends and the witnesses and it is those ripples she explores now in her darker fiction.<br />Teresa's books have been sold for translation in 15 languages. She lives in glorious Devon with her husband and two sons and blogs regularly about her "writing life" at her website - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.teresadriscoll.com">www.teresadriscoll.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9824054138692991517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
